        <meta property="og:url" content="https://pubs.acs.org/doi/full/10.1021/acs.langmuir.6b02870"><meta property="og:title" content="Synthesis of the Carbon-Coated Nanoparticle Co9S8 and Its Electrochemical Performance as an Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries"><meta property="og:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acs.langmuir.6b02870/asset/images/acs.langmuir.6b02870.social.jpeg_v03"><meta property="og:description" content="A Co9S8/C nanocomposite is prepared using a solid-state reaction followed by a facile mechanical ball-milling treatment, with sucrose as the carbon source. The phases, morphologies, and detailed structures of the Co9S8/C nanocomposite are well-characterized using X-ray diffraction (XRD), X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy, and high-resolution transmission electron microscopy. When evaluated as an anode material for sodium-ion batteries, the Co9S8/C nanocomposite electrode displays a reversible capacity of ∼567 mA h g–1 in the initial cycle and maintains a reversible capacity of ∼320 mA h g–1 after 30 cycles, indicating a larger capacity and a stable cycling performance. For comparison, the electrochemical performances of Co9S8 and Co9S8/C samples synthesized using the solid-state reaction are also displayed. The ex situ XRD and transmission electron microscopy tests demonstrate that Co9S8 undergoes a conversion-type sodium storage mechanism."><meta property="og:type" content="Article"><meta property="og:site_name" content="ACS Publications"><meta name="twitter:card" content="summary_large_image"><meta name="twitter:site" content="@ACSPublications"><meta name="twitter:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acs.langmuir.6b02870/asset/images/acs.langmuir.6b02870.social.jpeg_v03">

<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/wro/1122814~thiss-ds.js" async="" nonce="93187e3b3b48075b-SJC"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="93187e3b3b48075b-SJC">

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            timeout: 5000,

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
            },
            retrieveEntity: function (ms) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                if (ms == undefined || ms === '') {
                    ms = this.timeout;
                }

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res.data);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('failed to retrieve entity from local storage: ' + err);
                        });
                    // Set up the timeout
                    setTimeout(function () {
                        reject('Promise timed out ' + ms + ' ms');
                    }, ms);
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage due to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {
                            doi: doi,
                            entityid: entityId,
                            entityTitle: entityTitle,
                            eventGroupKey: '94c80531-3952-42b8-a1f6-c8d3dcbc5ebf'
                        }

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    }).fail(function (status) {
                        return reject(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (i = 0; i < allSsoInstitutions.length; i++) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        if(allSsoInstitutions.length === 0 && true){
                            self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, null, null)
                                .then(function () {
                                    console.log('No Entity found');
                                }, function (err) {
                                    console.log('failed to get the none entity status' ,err);
                                });
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            }).catch(function (err) {
                                reject(err);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();

                    if ($('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').length > 0) {
                        let institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox = $('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').get(0);
                        if (!$(institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox).is(":checked")) {
                            return;
                        }
                    }

                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="93187e3b3b48075b-SJC">
var dfpReady = false;
$(document).ready(function() {
    // var journalTitle = 'langmuir';
    var taxonomyKeywords = $('.article_header-taxonomy');
    var articleKeyword = $('meta[name="keywords"]');
    var articleTitle = $('meta[name="dc.Title"]');
    var articleDescription = $('meta[name="dc.Description"]');
    var abstractKeyword = $('p.articleBody_abstractText:contains("Keywords: ")');
    var searchTerms = [];

    if (taxonomyKeywords.length > 0) {
        $(taxonomyKeywords).children(".rlist--inline").children("li").each(function() {
            searchTerms.push($(this).text());
        });
    }
    else if (articleKeyword.length > 0) { 
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleKeyword.prop('content').split(', '));
    }
    else if (abstractKeyword.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(abstractKeyword.text().split("Keywords: ")[1].split('; '));
    }
    else if (articleDescription.length > 0) {
        $(articleDescription).each(function() {
            articleDescriptionKeywords = $(this).prop('content');
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/.,/g,"");
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/\s{2,}/g," ");
            searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleDescriptionKeywords.split(' '));
        });
    }

    if (articleTitle.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleTitle.prop('content').split(' '));
    }

    googletag.cmd.push(function() {
        var mappingLeader = googletag.sizeMapping().
        addSize([750, 200], [728, 90]). 
        addSize([0, 0], [320, 50]).
        build();
        //leaderboard
        googletag.defineSlot('/8868/journal/langmuir/article', [728, 90], 'dfp-journal-article-leaderboard').defineSizeMapping(mappingLeader).setTargeting('location', 'leaderboard1').setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //recommend
        googletag.defineSlot("/8868/journal/langmuir/article", [1, 1], "dfp-journal-article-recommend").setTargeting("ntvPlacement", ["1100167"]).setTargeting("location", "recommend").setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //googletag.pubads().enableSingleRequest();
        googletag.pubads().collapseEmptyDivs();
        googletag.pubads().setTargeting('inst',dartInstitutionType).setTargeting('memb',dartMember);
        googletag.pubads().addEventListener("slotRenderEnded", function(event) {
            console.log(event.slot.getSlotElementId() + " isEmpty: " + event.isEmpty + " | creative id: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            if((event.isEmpty === false) && (event.slot.getSlotElementId() != "dfp-journal-article-recommend")) {
                $("#" + event.slot.getSlotElementId()).parents(".advertisement").slideDown();
                console.log("ad display: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            }
            // else {
            //     console.log("no ad found");
            // }
        });
        googletag.enableServices();
        dfpReady = true;
    });
});
</script>

<script nonce="93187e3b3b48075b-SJC">
$(function() {
    var serialCode = "langd5";
    var books = ["reagents", "symposium", "advances", "medichemreviews", "styleguide"]
    if(books.includes(serialCode) === false) {
        // default click action
        $("[data-id]").on("mousedown", function(e) {
            var currentClickID = $(this).attr("data-id");

            if(currentClickID.includes("_hover") === false) {
                if(currentClickID.match("^article_") && !currentClickID.match("^article_abstract_CC")) {   
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Synthesis of the Carbon-Coated Nanoparticle Co&lt;sub&gt;9&lt;/sub&gt;S&lt;sub&gt;8&lt;/sub&gt; and Its Electrochemical Performance as an Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.langmuir.6b02870", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                }
            }
        });
        
        // Access Management icons hover
        var articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        var articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent === false) {
                articleAccessManagementIconHover = true;
                var articleAccessManagementHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleAccessManagementIconHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Synthesis of the Carbon-Coated Nanoparticle Co&lt;sub&gt;9&lt;/sub&gt;S&lt;sub&gt;8&lt;/sub&gt; and Its Electrochemical Performance as an Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.langmuir.6b02870", "Article_Element": articleAccessManagementHover });
    
                        articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        });
    
        // articleRightsPermissionsLink hover
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent === false) {
                articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = true;
                var articleRightsHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Synthesis of the Carbon-Coated Nanoparticle Co&lt;sub&gt;9&lt;/sub&gt;S&lt;sub&gt;8&lt;/sub&gt; and Its Electrochemical Performance as an Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.langmuir.6b02870", "Article_Element": articleRightsHover });
    
                        articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        });
    
        // Author hover
        var articleAuthorHover = false
        var articleAuthorHoverEvent = false
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if((articleAuthorHoverEvent === false) && ($(this).parent().hasClass("view-affs") === false)) {
                articleAuthorHover = true;
                var authorInfoHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAuthorHover === true) && (articleAuthorHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Synthesis of the Carbon-Coated Nanoparticle Co&lt;sub&gt;9&lt;/sub&gt;S&lt;sub&gt;8&lt;/sub&gt; and Its Electrochemical Performance as an Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.langmuir.6b02870", "Article_Element": authorInfoHover });
    
                        articleAuthorHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAuthorHover = false;
        });
    
        // CC License hover
        var articleAbstractCCHover = false
        var articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = false
        var articleDrawerCCHover = false
        var articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = false
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if($(this).attr("data-id")) {
                if(($(this).attr("data-id") === "article_drawer_CC-License") && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleDrawerCCHover = true;
                    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleDrawerCCHover === true) && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Synthesis of the Carbon-Coated Nanoparticle Co&lt;sub&gt;9&lt;/sub&gt;S&lt;sub&gt;8&lt;/sub&gt; and Its Electrochemical Performance as an Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.langmuir.6b02870", "Article_Element": "article_drawer_CC-License_hover" });
    
                            articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
                else if(($(this).attr("data-id").match("^article_abstract_CC")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleAbstractCCHover = true;
    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Synthesis of the Carbon-Coated Nanoparticle Co&lt;sub&gt;9&lt;/sub&gt;S&lt;sub&gt;8&lt;/sub&gt; and Its Electrochemical Performance as an Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.langmuir.6b02870", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                            articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
            }
            else if(($(this).hasClass("article__cc-license__link")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = true;
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Synthesis of the Carbon-Coated Nanoparticle Co&lt;sub&gt;9&lt;/sub&gt;S&lt;sub&gt;8&lt;/sub&gt; and Its Electrochemical Performance as an Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.langmuir.6b02870", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                        articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            if(articleAbstractCCHover === true) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = false;
            }
            if(articleDrawerCCHover = true) {
                articleDrawerCCHover = false;
            }
        });
        
        // show recommeneded click delay
        var intervalCount = 0;
        var showRecommendedInterval = setInterval(function() {
            intervalCount += 100;
            if($(".show-recommended__wrapper .show-recommended").length > 0) {
                clearInterval(showRecommendedInterval);
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowMore']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Synthesis of the Carbon-Coated Nanoparticle Co&lt;sub&gt;9&lt;/sub&gt;S&lt;sub&gt;8&lt;/sub&gt; and Its Electrochemical Performance as an Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.langmuir.6b02870", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowLess']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Synthesis of the Carbon-Coated Nanoparticle Co&lt;sub&gt;9&lt;/sub&gt;S&lt;sub&gt;8&lt;/sub&gt; and Its Electrochemical Performance as an Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.langmuir.6b02870", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
            }
        }, 100);
    }
});
</script>

class="articleMetrics_count"><h2>Citations</h2><div class="articleMetrics-val"><a href="#citeThis" class="internalNav">77</a></div></div></div></div><div class="articleMetrics_about"><div class="base data-db-target-of="aboutArticleMetrics" id="about-article-metrics" class="dropBlock__holder"><button class="articleMetrics_close"> <i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-close_thin"></i><span class="sr-only">close</span></button><p>Article Views are the COUNTER-compliant sum of full text article downloads since November 2008 (both PDF and HTML) across all institutions and individuals. These metrics are regularly updated to reflect usage leading up to the last few days.</p><p>Citations are the number of other articles citing this article, calculated by Crossref and updated daily.<a href="https://www.crossref.org/services/cited-by/"> Find more information about Crossref citation counts.</a></p><p>The Altmetric Attention Score is a quantitative measure of the attention that a research article has received online. Find more information on<a href="https://help.altmetric.com/support/solutions/articles/6000233311-how-is-the-altmetric-attention-score-calculated"> the Altmetric Attention Score and how the score is calculated.</a></p></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="article_abstract"><div class="article_abstract-title" id="Abstract" tabindex="0"><h2>Abstract</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div><div class="article_abstract-content hlFld-Abstract" id="abstractBox" property="description"><figure id="f_tgr1" data-index="0" class="article__inlineFigure article_abstract-img"><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img class="inline-fig internalNav" src="/cms/10.1021/acs.langmuir.6b02870/asset/images/medium/la-2016-02870t_0001.gif" alt="" id="tgr1" property="image" style="width:405px; height:275px"></button><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acs.langmuir.6b02870/asset/images/large/la-2016-02870t_0001.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acs.langmuir.6b02870&amp;id=f_tgr1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p class="articleBody_abstractText">A Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/C nanocomposite is prepared using a solid-state reaction followed by a facile mechanical ball-milling treatment, with sucrose as the carbon source. The phases, morphologies, and detailed structures of the Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/C nanocomposite are well-characterized using X-ray diffraction (XRD), X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy, and high-resolution transmission electron microscopy. When evaluated as an anode material for sodium-ion batteries, the Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/C nanocomposite electrode displays a reversible capacity of ∼567 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> in the initial cycle and maintains a reversible capacity of ∼320 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> after 30 cycles, indicating a larger capacity and a stable cycling performance. For comparison, the electrochemical performances of Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub> and Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/C samples synthesized using the solid-state reaction are also displayed. The ex situ XRD and transmission electron microscopy tests demonstrate that Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub> undergoes a conversion-type sodium storage mechanism.</p></div><div class="article__cc-license"><div class="article__cc-license__body"><p class="article__cc-license__para">This publication is licensed under the terms of your
                            institutional subscription.
                            <a href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D12593%26pageCount%3D10%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DXudong%2BLiu%252C%2BHuatao%2BLiu%252C%2BYanming%2BZhao%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D32%26issueNum%3D48%26contentID%3Dacs.langmuir.6b02870%26title%3DSynthesis%2Bof%2Bthe%2BCarbon-Coated%2BNanoparticle%2BCo9S8%2Band%2BIts%2BElectrochemical%2BPerformance%2Bas%2Ban%2BAnode%2BMaterial%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26numPages%3D10%26pa%3D%26issn%3D0743-7463%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Dlangd5%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D12602%26publicationDate%3DDecember%2B2016" class="link--bold">Request reuse permissions.</a></p></div></div><span class="hidden" property="publisher">ACS Publications</span><div class="article_header-article-copyright">Copyright © 2016 American Chemical Society</div><div class="article_header-footer-right"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone7" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone7"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div><div class="article__tags article__tags--subjects"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Subjects</h3><div tabindex="0" class="article__tags__tooltip"><div aria-describedby="tooltip-subjects" class="article__tags__icon"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are subjects</span></div><p id="tooltip-subjects" role="tooltip" class="article__tags__diff">
                                        Article subjects are automatically applied from the ACS Subject Taxonomy and describe the scientific concepts and themes of the article.</p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291337&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Carbon"> Carbon </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291371&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Electrodes"> Electrodes </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=292533&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Nanocomposites"> Nanocomposites </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=292439&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Physical and chemical processes"> Physical and chemical processes </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=292275&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Transmission electron microscopy"> Transmission electron microscopy </a></li></ul></div></div></div></div><div class="article_content"><div class="article_content-table hlFld-FullText"><div class="article_content-row"><div class="article_content-left" property="articleBody" style="width: 384px;"><div id="sec1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i1">1 Introduction</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">Although lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) have dominated the portable and smart electronics market over the past few decades, their large-scale applications in electric vehicles and stationary grid storage remain a challenge owing to limited energy density, high cost, and limited Li mineral reserves. Recently, sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have been considered to be an attractive alternative to LIBs because of the availability of rich sodium (Na) resources and outstanding chemical properties of the Na element similar to that of the alkaline family member of lithium (Li). <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1 ref2 ref3 ref4 ref5 ref6 ref7" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref1 ref2 ref3 ref4 ref5 ref6 ref7" aria-label="reference 1 to 7">(1-7)</a> At present, great efforts have been devoted to searching for promising electrode materials for SIBs. In the case of anode materials, significant progress has been made on hard carbon, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref8 ref9" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref8 ref9" aria-label="reference 8 and 9">(8, 9)</a> elements of group IV, such as Si, Ge, or Sn, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref10 ref11 ref12" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref10 ref11 ref12" aria-label="reference 10 to 12">(10-12)</a> intermetallic materials, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref13" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref13" aria-label="reference 13">(13)</a> metal sulfides, and various metal oxides. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref14 ref15" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref14 ref15" aria-label="reference 14 and 15">(14, 15)</a></div><div class="NLM_p">So far, the only commercialized sodium cell is the Na/S battery manufactured by NGK in Japan, which works at temperatures higher than 300 °C. The higher operating temperatures of the Na/S battery combined with the fragile β-alumina ceramic electrolyte separator have led many researchers to look for Na-based batteries with lower operating temperatures. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref16 ref17 ref18 ref19 ref20" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref16 ref17 ref18 ref19 ref20" aria-label="reference 16 to 20">(16-20)</a> Specifically, metal sulfides including Ni<sub>3</sub>S<sub>2</sub>, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref21" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref21" aria-label="reference 21">(21)</a> MoS<sub>2</sub>, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref22 ref23 ref24 ref25" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref22 ref23 ref24 ref25" aria-label="reference 22 to 25">(22-25)</a> SnS<sub>2</sub>, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref26 ref27 ref28" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref26 ref27 ref28" aria-label="reference 26 to 28">(26-28)</a> SnS, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref26 ref29" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref26 ref29" aria-label="reference 26 and 29">(26, 29)</a> Fe<sub>2</sub>S, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref30" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref30" aria-label="reference 30">(30)</a> and Sb<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref31" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref31" aria-label="reference 31">(31)</a> have been recently identified to be promising candidates for SIBs because of their high specific theoretical capacities and low cost. However, it has been found that, based on a conversion reaction process, metal sulfides can form the metal and sodium sulfides during the sodiation/desodiation process, which will easily result in voltage hysteresis, volume change, and low initial Coulomb efficiency, thus leading to poor electrochemical performance. To improve the electrochemical performance of metal sulfides, many strategies have been employed, such as construction of optimized structures, decreasing the particle size, and carbon coating on the surface of metal sulfides, as well as addition of fluoroethylene carbonate (FEC) in the electrolyte. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref32 ref33 ref34" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref32 ref33 ref34" aria-label="reference 32 to 34">(32-34)</a> Recently, to accommodate the volume expansion, Li and co-workers prepared a carbon nanotube (CNT)-encapsulated Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub> anode for SIBs, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref35" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref35" aria-label="reference 35">(35)</a> and the results from the <i>in</i>-situ transmission electron microscopy (TEM) suggest that the volume expansion of Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub> can be controlled by the CNT during the sodiation and desodiation processes. However, no further research on the electrochemical performance of Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, including galvanostatic discharge/charge cycles, cycling performance, and electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) tests, has been reported yet.</div><div class="NLM_p last">To further investigate the electrochemical performance of Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, herein, we synthesize a carbon-coated nanoparticle of Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub> composite (the Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/C nanocomposite) by ball-milling Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub> in the presence of sucrose as the carbon source. The electrochemical performance is found to be good, which is attributed to the small particle size of Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub> (&lt;100 nm) and the amorphous carbon coating on its surface with a thickness of just about 5 nm. The small particle size is beneficial to the quick penetration of the electrolyte and the short distance of lithium ion diffusion, whereas the carbon coating film favors the electron transport and accommodates the volume expansion/contraction of the nanocomposite during the discharge/charge process.</div></div><div id="sec2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i2">2 Experimental Section</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div id="sec2-1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i3" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i3">2.1 Synthesis of the Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/C Nanocomposite</h3><div class="NLM_p last">The carbon-coated Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/C nanoparticles were prepared using a solid-state reaction followed by a ball-milling treatment as described below. An appropriate ratio of dried Co<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> (4.4676 g) and S (6 g) powders (Co:S = 1:3.5 in mol, sulfur excess) and sucrose (5.2338 g, 50 wt % of the total mass of Co<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> and S) as the carbon source were mixed thoroughly using an agate mortar. The mixture was annealed at 500 °C for 12 h in a temperature-controlled quartz tube furnace under an ambience of Ar/H<sub>2</sub> (70/30 in volume percent) to obtain the Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/C composite. To obtain the Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/C nanocomposite, the resultant product was subjected to planetary ball milling (Pulverisette 7, Fritsch) for 240 h at 500 rpm using a steel jar and balls under an air atmosphere. Every 30 min of ball milling was followed by a 15 min break to release the heat. The process for fabricating a carbon-free Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub> sample was the same as that for the preparation of Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/C, just without the carbon source.</div></div><div id="sec2-2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i4" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i4">2.2 Physical Characterization</h3><div class="NLM_p last">The X-ray diffraction data (XRD) for the analysis were collected using a Bruker D8 advance diffractometer with Cu Kα radiation. A graphite monochromator was used for diffracted beams, and a step-scan mode was adopted with a scanning step of 0.02. The <i>Rietveld</i> refinements of pure single-phase Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub> were carried out using the GSAS program (Larson &amp; Von Dreele, 2000) <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref36" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref36" aria-label="reference 36">(36)</a> via the EXPGUI interface (Toby, 2001). <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref37" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref37" aria-label="reference 37">(37)</a> The carbon content was verified using a Vario EL (Elementar, Germany) CHNS elemental analyzer. Thermogravimetry analysis (TGA) curves were collected using an STA-449-F3 thermal analyzer (NETZSCH, Germany), with a heating rate of 10 °C/min in the temperature range 25–800 °C under an air atmosphere. X-ray photo-electron spectroscopy (XPS) images were obtained using a Kratos Axis Ultra spectrometer. Scanning electron microscopy (SEM) images of these composites were obtained using a Nova NanoSEM 430 (FEI, USA) scanning electron microscope, and the microstructures were observed using a high-resolution transmission electron microscope (Hitachi 7650) operating at 200 kV. The energy-dispersive X-ray (EDX) analysis was performed using the EDX system attached to the electron microscopes.</div></div><div id="sec2-3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i5" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i5">2.3 Electrochemical Testing</h3><div class="NLM_p last">The electrochemical properties of the three samples were evaluated with two-electrode electrochemical cells using an automatic battery tester system (Land, China). The anode films were prepared by mixing the as-synthesized sample with a polyvinylidiene fluoride (PVDF) binder and acetylene black in a weight ratio of 7:2:1 in <i>N</i>-methyl-2-pyrrolidone (NMP). The obtained slurries were coated on a Cu foil uniformly, and 3 mg of active materials was loaded onto the electrodes. The two-electrode electrochemical cells were assembled in a Mikrouna glove box filled with ultrahigh argon. Sodium metal foils were used as counter electrodes, a glass fiber was used as the separator, and 1 M NaPF<sub>6</sub> in EC (ethylene carbonate)/DMC (dimethyl carbonate) (1:1 vol %) with 5 wt % additive FEC was used as the electrolyte. EIS measurements were taken on an Autolab PGSTAT302N potentiostat (Metrohm, Netherlands). The impedance spectra were recorded by applying an ac voltage of 5 mV in the frequency range 1–0.01 Hz.</div></div></div><div id="sec3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i6">3 Results and Discussion</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">To obtain the structural parameters accurately, the XRD data of carbon-free Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub> were used to carry out the structure refinement. It is worth noting that a higher amount of sulfur is needed in our precursor mixture in consideration of the sulfur mass loss caused by sublimation during the annealing process. <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig1" aria-label="Figure 1">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>a shows the <i>Rietveld</i> refinement results of Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, and a cube space group of <i>Fm</i>3̅<i>m</i> (ICSD card No. 657415) is chosen as the structural refinement model. The reasonably small <i>R</i><sub>wp</sub> factor (7.65%) suggests that single-phase Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub> can be obtained under our experimental process. The unit cell parameter is <i>a</i> = 9.926(2) Å, and the atomic sites with the coordinates of Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub> determined from the <i>Rietveld</i> refinement are listed in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#tbl1" aria-label="Table 1">Table </a><a class="ref showTableEvent internalNav" data-id="tbl1" href="#tbl1">1</a>. <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig1" aria-label="Figure 1">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>b shows the schematic crystal structure of Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub> based on further information from the XRD pattern. The structure consists of two polyhedrons including a CoS<sub>6</sub> octahedron and a CoS<sub>4</sub> tetrahedron, where each CoS<sub>6</sub> octahedron shares its six corners with twenty-four CoS<sub>4</sub> tetrahedrons. Nine cobalt atoms per formula occupy two Wyckoff positions Co1 (4b) and Co2 (32f), and eight sulfur atoms also occupy two different Wyckoff positions S1 (8c) and S2 (24e). Co1 is coordinated by six S2 atoms forming the CoS<sub>6</sub> octahedron, and Co2 is coordinated by one S1 atom and three S2 atoms, forming a distorted CoS<sub>4</sub> tetrahedron. The different Co–S lengths including Co1–S2 (2.34 Å), Co2–S1 (2.12 Å), and Co2–S2 (2.23 Å) have different bond energies, which might determine the sequence of chemical bond breaking during the sodiation process discussed below.</div><figure id="fig1" data-index="1" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 1</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acs.langmuir.6b02870/asset/images/medium/la-2016-02870t_0009.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acs.langmuir.6b02870/asset/images/large/la-2016-02870t_0009.jpeg" id="gr1" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 1. (a) <i>Rietveld</i> analysis of carbon-free Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub> and (b) schematic structure of cube Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub>.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acs.langmuir.6b02870/asset/images/large/la-2016-02870t_0009.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acs.langmuir.6b02870&amp;id=fig1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_table-wrap" id="tbl1"><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption"><div class="NLM_caption" id=""><div class="title2">Table 1. Atomic Sites and Coordinates of Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub> Determined From the <i>Rietveld</i> Refinement</div></div></div><div class="scrollable-table-wrap" style="display: block;"><table class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">1.021(11)</td></tr><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="row" align="left">Co (2)</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0"
